<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background: #f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/44px-Wikipedia-logo.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/66px-Wikipedia-logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wikipedia-logo.png/88px-Wikipedia-logo.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></div></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> has an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/religion" class="extiw" title="w:religion">religion</a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/religion" class="extiw" title="w:religion">Wikipedia </a></span></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Religions_4x5.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Religions_4x5.png/120px-Religions_4x5.png" decoding="async" width="120" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Religions_4x5.png/180px-Religions_4x5.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Religions_4x5.png/240px-Religions_4x5.png 2x" data-file-width="737" data-file-height="915" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Religions_4x5.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Religion symbols</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_forms">Alternative forms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Alternative forms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/Religion#English" title="Religion">Religion</a></span></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Norman_language" class="extiw" title="w:Anglo-Norman language">Anglo-Norman</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro"><a href="/wiki/religiun#Old_French" title="religiun">religiun</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro"><a href="/wiki/religion#Old_French" title="religion">religion</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la"><a href="/wiki/religio#Latin" title="religio">religiō</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">scrupulousness, pious misgivings, superstition, conscientiousness, sanctity, an object of veneration, cult-observance, reverence</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Most likely from the <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages" class="extiw" title="w:Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a></span></span> root <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h%E2%82%82leg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h₂leg (page does not exist)">*h₂leg</a></i> with the meanings preserved in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la"><a href="/wiki/diligere#Latin" title="diligere">dīligere</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="la"><a href="/wiki/legere#Latin" title="legere">legere</a></i> (“to read repeatedly”, “to have something solely in mind”).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Noun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">religion</strong> (<i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#countable" title="Appendix:Glossary">countable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/religions#English" title="religions">religions</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The <a href="/wiki/belief" title="belief">belief</a> in a reality beyond what is <a href="/wiki/perceptible" title="perceptible">perceptible</a> by the <a href="/wiki/sense" title="sense">senses</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/practice" title="practice">practices</a> associated with this belief.
<span class="HQToggle"><a>quotations ▼</a></span><dl><dd><i>My brother tends to value <b>religion</b>, but my sister not as much.</i></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1902</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_James" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William James">William James</a>, <i>The Varieties of Religious Experience</i>, Lecture 2:
<dl><dd>Most books on the philosophy of <b>religion</b> try to begin with a precise definition of what its essence consists of. ... I shall not be pedantic enough to enumerate any of them to you now. Meanwhile the very fact that they are so many and so different from one another is enough to prove that the word “<b>religion</b>” cannot stand for any single principle or essence, but is rather a collective name.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#countable" title="Appendix:Glossary">countable</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A particular system of such <a href="/wiki/belief" title="belief">belief</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/ritual" title="ritual">rituals</a> and <a href="/wiki/practice" title="practice">practices</a> proper to it.
<dl><dd><i>Islam is a major <b>religion</b> in parts of Asia and Africa.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Eckankar is a new <b>religion</b> but Zoroastrianism is an old <b>religion</b>.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The way of life committed to by <a href="/wiki/monks" title="monks">monks</a> and <a href="/wiki/nuns" title="nuns">nuns</a>.
<dl><dd><i>The monk entered <b>religion</b> when he was 20 years of age.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#countable" title="Appendix:Glossary">countable</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any practice to which someone or some group is seriously <a href="/wiki/devoted" title="devoted">devoted</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a>quotations ▼</a></span><dl><dd><i>At this point, </i>Star Trek<i> has really become a <b>religion</b>.</i></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1985</b>,  Joan Morrison,  <cite>Share House Blues</cite>, Boolarong Publications, page 97:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">'Religion can't exist without mystery, especially science, the newest <b>religion</b>.'</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#obsolete" title="Appendix:Glossary">obsolete</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Faithfulness to a given <a href="/wiki/principle" title="principle">principle</a>; <a href="/wiki/conscientiousness" title="conscientiousness">conscientiousness</a>. <span class="defdate">[16th-17th c.]</span>
<span class="HQToggle"><a>quotations ▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1603</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Florio" class="extiw" title="w:John Florio">John Florio</a>, transl.; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michel_de_Montaigne" class="extiw" title="w:Michel de Montaigne">Michel de Montaigne</a>,  chapter 8, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Essays_(Montaigne)" class="extiw" title="w:Essays (Montaigne)">The Essayes,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="or, Morall, Politike and Millitarie Discourses of Lo. Michaell de Montaigne, Knight of the Noble Order of St. Michaell, and One of the Gentlemen in Ordinary of the French King, Henry the Third His Chamber">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite>, book II, printed at London: By <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valentine_Simmes" class="extiw" title="w:Valentine Simmes">Val[entine] Simmes</a> for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Edward Blount</a><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="dwelling in Paules churchyard">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/946730821">946730821</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Oh with what <b>religion</b> doe I respect and observe the same!</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Usage notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>Generally speaking, certain groups that do not acknowledge the existence of one or more <a href="/wiki/deity" title="deity">deities</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, are still religious—though some prefer a definition of religion without non-theistic groups within the definition.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Verb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">religion</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3|s|pres-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/religions#English" title="religions">religions</a></b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/religioning#English" title="religioning">religioning</a></b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past|and|past|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/religioned#English" title="religioned">religioned</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Engage in <a href="/wiki/religious" title="religious">religious</a> <a href="/wiki/practice" title="practice">practice</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a>quotations ▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1978</b>,  <cite>Military Chaplains' Review</cite>, page 70:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">On the scales below, circle the one ( + ) or (-) number which best represents your situation on both the belief and practice dimensions for each of the traditional and nontraditional forms of <b>religioning</b>.</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2013</b>,  Monica R. Miller,  <cite>Religion and Hip Hop</cite>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415628571" title="Special:BookSources/0415628571">→ISBN</a></small>, page 74:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">A similar caution is made by Nye when he calls for a re-evaluation of the category of religion in relationship to theory and method, suggesting that this category: be reconstructed in terms of practice theory as religious practice or <b>religioning</b>.</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b>,  Alexander Horstmann &amp; ‎Jin-Heon Jung,  <cite>Building Noah’s Ark for Migrants, Refugees, and Religious Communities</cite>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1137496304" title="Special:BookSources/1137496304">→ISBN</a></small>, page 13:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Religious practice and action (“<b>religioning</b>”) can be liberating, and can connect displaced people with the spirits of home.</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/indoctrinate" title="indoctrinate">Indoctrinate</a> into a specific religion.
<span class="HQToggle"><a>quotations ▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><b>1890</b>, John R. Kelso, Deity analyzed: In six lectures - Page 37
<dl><dd>To men whose minds are thus <b>religioned</b>, tied back to gods that never advance, there can never be any such word as progress</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2007</b>,  Janette Oke,  <cite>A Bride for Donnigan</cite>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0764202502" title="Special:BookSources/0764202502">→ISBN</a></small>, page 225:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">“What do you do, Donnigan? Spend all yer time <b>religioning</b> yer young?”</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>To make <a href="/wiki/sacred" title="sacred">sacred</a> or <a href="/wiki/symbolic" title="symbolic">symbolic</a>; <a href="/wiki/sanctify" title="sanctify">sanctify</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a>quotations ▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1994</b>,  Timothy Morton,  <cite>Shelley and the Revolution in Taste</cite>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521471354" title="Special:BookSources/0521471354">→ISBN</a></small>, page 238:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The discussion of diet and health raises the question of the importance of discussing vegetarianism in relation to the contemporary <b>religioning</b> of health; as Ross remarks, 'health has replaced sexuality as the new privileged discourse of bodily truth and inner essence'.</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>2011</b>, Andrew O'Shea, Pedagogy, Oppression and Transformation in a 'Post-Critical' Climate, p 116
<dl><dd>The ideas expressed above challenge us to continuously rupture and interrupt racialized, classed, gendered, <b>religioned</b> and sexualized norms that inhere between and within institutions, understandings of bodies and our Selves.</dd></dl></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2013</b>,  Andrew Kam-Tuck Yip &amp; Stephen Hunt,  <cite>The Ashgate Research Companion to Contemporary Religion and Sexuality</cite>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1409472256" title="Special:BookSources/1409472256">→ISBN</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">If queer Jews, Muslims and Christians are engaged in queering their religions, they are also engaged in what might becalled '<b>religioning'</b> the queer.</span> </div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=religion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
